  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText17252910597527006174" style="display:none"><i>An alternate cover edition for this ISBN13 can be found <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29612615-poison-princess" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</i><br /><br /><b>She could save the world—or destroy it.</b><br /><br />Sixteen-year-old Evangeline "Evie" Greene leads a charmed life, until she begins experiencing horrifying hallucinations. When an apocalyptic event decimates her Louisiana hometown, Evie realizes her hallucinations were actually visions of the future—and they're still happening. Fighting for her life and desperate for answers, she must turn to her wrong-side-of-the-bayou classmate: Jack Deveaux.<br /><br /><b>But she can't do either alone.</b><br /><br />With his mile-long rap sheet, wicked grin, and bad attitude, Jack is like no boy Evie has ever known. Even though he once scorned her and everything she represented, he agrees to protect Evie on her quest. She knows she can't totally depend on Jack. If he ever cast that wicked grin her way, could she possibly resist him?<br /><br /><b>Who can Evie trust?</b><br /><br />As Jack and Evie race to find the source of her visions, they meet others who have gotten the same call. An ancient prophesy is being played out, and Evie is not the only one with special powers. A group of twenty-two teens has been chosen to reenact the ultimate battle between good and evil. But it's not always clear who is on which side.</span>

<div id="review_2803074898" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2803074898" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2803074898?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781481426664" href="/book/show/20759393-poison-princess">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=ya-series">ya-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2803074898" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1928862248817429017"><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567369933i/28085397._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote><b>Didn't enjoy this one nearly as much as I thought I would. </b><br/><br/>It's probably a case of <s>it's not you, it's me.</s> <br/><br/>Eff it. Okay. I'm gonna get real here. <br/><br/>It's you (book).<b> Totally all on you.</b><br/><br/>We start with a sterotypical white, blond <b>Pretty-Pretty girl </b>who <b>
  <i>tragically</i>
</b> has "mental health issues".<br/><br/>Essentially, this girl is either A) hallucinating or B) can read the future, control plants, heal herself, make her fingers into claws, and other godlike powers<b>. 50/50</b><br/><br/>Meds are thrown away, counselling not an </span>
  <span id="freeText1928862248817429017" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567369933i/28085397._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><b>Didn't enjoy this one nearly as much as I thought I would. </b><br><br>It's probably a case of <s>it's not you, it's me.</s> <br><br>Eff it. Okay. I'm gonna get real here. <br><br>It's you (book).<b> Totally all on you.</b><br><br>We start with a sterotypical white, blond <b>Pretty-Pretty girl </b>who <b>
  <i>tragically</i>
</b> has "mental health issues".<br><br>Essentially, this girl is either A) hallucinating or B) can read the future, control plants, heal herself, make her fingers into claws, and other godlike powers<b>. 50/50</b><br><br>Meds are thrown away, counselling not an option, leaving the audience to wonder if it's real or if <b> it is all in her head </b>.<br><br>Then there's the <b>Psycho </b>- totally evil but in a hot way. (And he's close enough in age to Pretty-Pretty so it's not creepy). Psycho keeps girls in his basement for his "experiments."<br><br>(One such experiment - I kid you not - is creating<b> a sodium chloride concoction </b>AKA a salt spray b/c the evil post-apocalyptic monsters can't stand table salt. <b>
  <i>Mmmmhmmm...</i>
</b>)<br><br>Anyway, <b>Psycho lures Pretty-Pretty </b>into his house and makes her drink sleepy tea and spends the book alternating between <b>EXTREMELY </b>murderous thoughts and <b> WOW</b> she's kinda hawt.<br><br>Meanwhile,<b> Pretty-Pretty tells him her entire life story</b>...which can be boiled down to: <br><br>--I'm super pretty and yet I just don't fit in!<br>--I have super cool powers and yet no one understands me!<br>--The super-cute teenage alcoholic likes me and yet I'm soooo alonnnnnne!<br>--My nickname is Sugar Tits, wahhhhhh!<br>--Teen Drunk survived the apocalypse to save me, do I give him my V card???<br><br><b>
  <u>Rinse and repeat.</u>
</b><br><br><b>On a side note -</b> while I seriously questioned everything that came out of Pretty-Pretty's mouth, I really didn't get her constant jumping to get in a motorized vehicle with Teen Drunk. He literally drank more than he breathed.<br><b><br>On another side note </b>- at one point, we pick up an autistic teen who's (and note the irritation) adorably whimsical, sweetly innocent and wise beyond his years. <br><br>Can we have a SINGLE YA book that doesn't <b>use mental illness or autism as a cool/trendy way </b>to further the plot? No? Fab.<br><br>Anyway, the book really just <b>meanders through Pretty-Pretty's life </b> (ironically, she supposedly told Psycho this in a single evening in a very drugged state...the audiobook took over 12.5 hours and she spoke slow as molasses whenever we would cut to her...so really? Really now.). <br><br>To be fair, there's <b>some weak backstory</b> about the origin of her powers (loosely associated with tarot cards) but it really was just 12 hrs of <b>Pretty-Pretty wandering</b> into danger, being saved by Teen Drunk, being chased by rapey men (because everyone knows the first thing that happens in the apocalypse is the whole "<b>we gotta repopulate the earth</b>" scenario).<br><br>Well...ok. That's not ALL there is to the book. <br><br>I would be doing this book a disservice if I didn't mention <b>
  <i>the teenage hormones. </i>
</b><br><br>Whenever Pretty-Pretty wasn't complaining or staring at a mirror, she spent her time<b> having savagely lustful thoughts </b>about Teen Drunk and insisting that she wants her "first time" to be special. <br><br>Puh-lease. Gurl. <br><br>This is the APOCALYPSE. <br><br>You'd think that literally everyone you know dying, monsters chasing behind every corner and weird nightmare dreams would probably be sufficient of a downer to quell some of this...apparently not. <br><br>I'm just saying <b>do we need tensions to get needle-sharp </b>EVERY time he reaches up and a sliver of his washboard abs is visible? <br><br>Apparently, yes. That is the only reasonable reaction after your BFF dies. <br><br>AND THEN there's Teen Drunk who is so manipulative, vindictive, passive-aggressive, aggressive, horny (etc) that you really wonder what Pretty-Pretty sees in him. <br><br>Oh wait. <br><br>I know.<br><br><b>He's like <i>so</i> totally hawt</b> (*fans self*) that it's worth it.<br><br>He's a bad boy with a <b>
  <i>sensitive soul</i>
</b> raised on the wrong side of the tracks who needs saving! If only Pretty-Pretty sticks with Teen Drunk, she can totally change him from a lowlife to a decent and loving human being!!<br><br>Gag.<br><br>All in all, this one was <b>every bit as annoying</b> as Jill (my friend from TCE Bookclub) told me it would be. You were right in every sense of the word.<br><br><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br>Surprisingly well-read! And I really mean it. This reader really did a great job with the tone and inflection. So many times I end up hating the reader when I listen to a bad book - not this time. <br><br>Just checked on the reader - it was Emma Gavin. Gosh. If I had a nickel for every audiobook read by her I'd have...about $1.45. Still. This girl knows how to read a book. Wonderful job.Two thumbs up for the quality!<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1928862248817429017" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_434653665" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/434653665" />
    <a title="Tomoe Hotaru" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5548051-tomoe-hotaru"><img alt="Tomoe Hotaru" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571221863p2/5548051.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/434653665?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tomoe Hotaru" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tomoe Hotaru" href="/user/show/5548051-tomoe-hotaru">Tomoe Hotaru</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=craptastic">craptastic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=zzzzzzz">zzzzzzz</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer434653665" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9844553949789557026"><b>
  <u>04 Oct. '19</u>
</b><br/><b>Hold up!</b> before you decide to post a comment professing your undying love for this book; of how utterly wrong I am about Jackson because he's actually seriously like super hot and this is what girls like you fall for or something; or how the beginning of this book completely works for you because of <b>reasons</b>; <i>please</i> don't. Because, umm, I don't care? Ha. Like, write it in your own review. <b>K thx bye.</b><br/><br/><b>
  <u>11 Oct. '14</u>
</b><br/>For those who have read the 2nd book and can confirm things for me, h</span>
  <span id="freeText9844553949789557026" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>04 Oct. '19</u>
</b><br><b>Hold up!</b> before you decide to post a comment professing your undying love for this book; of how utterly wrong I am about Jackson because he's actually seriously like super hot and this is what girls like you fall for or something; or how the beginning of this book completely works for you because of <b>reasons</b>; <i>please</i> don't. Because, umm, I don't care? Ha. Like, write it in your own review. <b>K thx bye.</b><br><br><b>
  <u>11 Oct. '14</u>
</b><br>For those who have read the 2nd book and can confirm things for me, here are <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/751013156" rel="nofollow noopener">my predictions on Endless Knight</a>.<br><br><b>
  <u>19 Oct. '12</u>
</b><br><b>Be forewarned!</b> There shall be a lot of cussing and angriness and bitch-slapping in this review. If you are a fan of this book/author, or/and not a fan of cuss words in reviews, I highly advise you not to read as I do not want to offend anyone.<br><br>**********<br><br>Like an old, dying, rheumatic ox plowing through a field of mud and shit. All for the promises of a harvest of fresh, delicious, sweetcorn that he will never ever enjoy. That is how I felt as I trudged through this ...... this heap of stink. <i>Plod, plod, plod,</i> and how many times I'd found myself in the middle of this dreck; dirt behind me, dirt before me, dirt all around me -- but my feet were already wet and icky, and <i>sweetcorn!</i> You promised there'd be sweetcorn!<br>Alas, no sweetcorn for me. Not even one lousy cob. Maybe there will be in the future, but I'm not sinking my hooves in more shit and risking it a <i>second</i> time.<br><br>You were promised a (post-)apocalyptic. <b>You will not get a post-apocalyptic</b> before you trudge through half a field of shit. The first chapter -- prologue? It was a right hooker. Totally sucked me in. Even though I had my consternations -- this vaguely rapey vibe didn't settle down too good in my stomach. <br>But it promised action! Mystery! Everything on the blurb!<br>So you read on, all jittery and drooling for sweetcorn ...... and then you're slapped with <i>
  <b>thirteen whole chapters of teenage high school drama</b>
</i> that has NOTHING! <i>no importance whatsoever</i> to the plot.<br><br>First of all, these thirteen chapters was a <i>recount</i>. Our protagonist, Evie, wandered into a house and was asked to recount her journey. And she did exactly that. <b>In excruciatingly painful detail</b> we would be told of her last <i>seven whole frigging days</i> before the cataclysmic event that hit the entire planet.<br>So that is <i>thirteen chapters</i> reading about her rich-girl life in her rich-girl school, with all the rich-girl brand names being splattered like rainbow gifs constantly in your face. <b>Constantly!</b> See, <b>
  <u>this is the first nonsensical part of this novel</u>
</b> -- how the bloody hell do you <i>remember</i> seven entire days in such minute detail, especially <i>months</i> after it even happened?!<br><br>No matter. Let's assume she has super-special memory. The second issue I have with this is <b>priority in story-telling</b>, people! Why the <i>fuck</i> do I care about your surprise party? Promising your V-card to your boyfriend? Your grades drama?<br>Why the hell would you spend <i>thirteen whole chapters</i> telling us about this honest-to-God perfect jock boyfriend and strangely devoted best friend, when <i>none of that matters?!</i><br>Read it. Go on, read it, and tell me why the hell knowing Brandon or Mel or even Evie's entire bloody life was important. Spoiler, people: THEY DIED! WE SEE NONE OF THEM EVER AGAIN! <b>
  <u>They had no relevancy to the story at all!</u>
</b><br>I just ploughed through that field of shit AND YOU AIN'T EVEN GONNA USE IT?! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381731578ra/5244821.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I want to slap a bitch. And I don't <i>care</i> if in the sequels Brandon magically turns out to have survived. In fact, I wouldn't be surprised if that indeed happened. Point is, you could've glossed over all of that high school drama bullshit and got on to the <b>meat</b> of the story without wasting all that damn paper!<br><br>But do you know what <i>did</i> get glossed over? <b>Two hundred and fourteen days of cataclysmic action.</b> I'm sorry, let me get this straight. You told us, in detail, seven days' worth of your text messages, your pathetic visions in school, your scribbling drawings that I don't give a rat's arse about, your worrying about having sex for the first time, your petty pseudo-racist drama against the new kids in school -- but then after the cataclysmic event, you <i>jumped ahead four months</i> and all of a sudden we have cannibals, pseudo-zombies, militia men, and none of that is explained?<br><u>
  <b>The story-telling was imbalanced and the prioritizing sucked</b>
</u> to be awfully straightforward with you. <br><br>Third issue that frequently made me want to ragequit was the <u>
  <b>absolute laziness of the worldbuilding</b>
</u>.<br>How did these zombies come about?! Apparently, humans suddenly <i>mutated</i> (because of ... the sun? The thirst? The sheer stupidity of this book?!) and became attracted to water and hated the sun. Because prophecy!<br>Apparently all plants and water and "everything organic" was obliterated off the face of the earth, but buildings and houses still stood perfectly well. And of course, <i>some</i> water sources remained in tact. Because special!<br>Apparently everyone who was outdoors died during the big flash and explosion, but everyone <i>in</i>doors were unharmed. Because sunburst can't penetrate walls, y'all!<br>I realize that Evie wouldn't have known any of the answers to these logic flaws, but -- the fact that these questions even existed wasn't even <i>touched upon</i> by the characters! No one questions why only plants and animals suddenly turned to dust. Or why buildings stayed in tact. Or why <i>anything</i>! They just took it for granted:<br><blockquote>
  <i>Some say the very tilt of the earth's axis wobbled, disturbing the balance of our world, lowering its defenses. Others claim that the depleted ozone layer--already a peeling scab--ripped open, leaving us vulnerable to heat and radiation.</i>
</blockquote><br>Yes, of course, because the tilt of the earth could somehow shift and <i>buildings</i> remain perfectly well.<br><blockquote>
  <i>"I'm in your camp. Best not to obsess over it."</i>
</blockquote><br>And <i>that</i> is how the author attempts to brush it aside and have <i>us</i> "not obsess over it".<br><br>You might argue, this was a romance, after all, so I shouldn't expect much in the way of action or whatevs. And I'd say sure, it's a romance. But then puh-<i>lease</i> do not delude the market into thinking this is a post-apocalyptic YA adventure. Boy am I sick of dystopia/P-A and YA being used to market a book. Look. The truth is <b>
  <u>the post-apocalyptic elements in <i>Poison Princess</i> could have been taken away and it wouldn't have mattered</u>
</b>.<br>I saw P-A here being used as an <i>excuse</i> to have our teens running rampant without parental control, journeying across states or whatever. I saw it as a pathetic plot progression tool. The world could have still been in tact, no cataclysmic event, and these kids and Evie's whole <i>task</i> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[of killing every other Major Arcana tarot card or whatever <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> could still exist.<br>As it were, there was no real purpose of having a cataclysmic event hit the face of the earth, other than to prove that Evie and her grandmother weren't insane.<br><br>But while we're on the subject -- <u>
  <b>even as a <i>romance</i>, this book failed me</b>
</u>. There was nothing to like about Jackson. He's a rude, crass, insensitive asshole, whose only attraction to Evie was <i>literally</i> based on her wriggling arse and pretty face. No joke.<br>The rest of the characters were so blah it's not even worth mentioning. <i>All</i> the boys only wanted sex, all the girls only too willing to lap up guys' attention. And <i>of course</i> after the apocalypse, virtually all men turned into pseudo-zombies, cannibals, or lawless men who, upon seeing a girl, can only think of sexing her up.<br>Because we're animals like that and we have no self-control, you know. And also because <b>Kresley Cole</b>'s understanding of human psychology isn't really up to scratch.<br><br>Basically, <u>
  <b>all the characters were unlikable and unrelatable</b>
</u>. Let's start with Evie ... oh, I could go on forever about her, but I'll try to keep it brief. She was a popular girl, and everyone's lives revolve around her <i>so much</i> that the entire school knows when she's about to lose her virginity. Every man who sees her <i>leers</i> at her "as if they'd never seen a girl before". <br>She's one of the richest people in town -- the richest being her jock boyfriend, Brandon, who picks her up in a Porsche? Jaguar? something like that -- and was <i>faithful to her</i> while she was away, so she has to give him her virginity <i>as a reward</i> because damn how else is a girl gonna keep her man?<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>She's <i>so</i> popular she <i>waves at everyone</i> and stops by every group of people on her way into school because the school would <i>collapse</i> if she didn't play Miss Congeniality. No, seriously.<br><blockquote>
  <i>"If popularity is your My-Little-Pony gundrop-forest of a dream, then so be it. Who am I to piss on your dreams? But know this: The school would freaking shut down without you(...)"</i>
</blockquote><br><br>So yeah, meet Mary Sue.<br><br>Her best friend was just as unlikable.<br><blockquote>
  <i>"You have two choices, grasshopper. Out-slut Clotile--or go Springer on her ass. I'm down for the assist in both scenarios."</i>
</blockquote><br>Umm, how about get a boyfriend who doesn't <i>care</i> how sexy other girls are dressed?!<br><br>Also:<br><blockquote>
  <i>Mel waved away my concerns. "Ignore your mom, put out for Brandon, tank your grades. If you fail, I'll flunk with you."</i>
</blockquote><br>Yep, that's her endorsing Evie to give up her virginity so Brandon would stop looking at another girl.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381731578ra/5244823.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But let's get technical now, shall we? Because in this aspect, <i>Poison Princess</i> also sucked bad. The <b>
  <u>pacing was poor and off-beat</u>
</b>. Again, this had a lot to do with priorities. Seriously, there is this one chapter, where basically Evie tells her love-interest, Jackson, also in detail, about her past. About her asylum days, about her grandma, about the voices she hears ...... all of this <i>we already know</i> and yet we had to read about it all. over. a-fucking-gain!<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>All the "romance" drama were expanded upon in minute detail, even running out of gas took one too many pages of attention, and the action scenes were too few and far between and <i>piss poor</i> it was hardly worth the wait.<br><br>Another technical thing I <i>really</i> found disrupting was the dialogue. Because Jackson is Cajun, he slips in french phrases and words in his dialogue. Often. And every time, Evie would translate it to us. Yeah, I know, if she doesn't, most of us probably wouldn't understand it. But hell, none of those phrases were even important. I don't get why it needed to be there in the first place. Authenticity? Actually, it made it sound pretentious if anything.<br><br>So <b>there was nothing that redeemed this book for me</b>. Nothing. I used to think <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/172807749" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Vampire Academy</i>
</a> by <b>Richelle Mead</b> was the crappiest book I ever wasted money on, but that title is now replaced.<br>I saw this as a vague attempt of another <a href="http://elfswood.blogspot.com/2012/05/angelfall.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Angelfall</i>
</a> type of book, but it fell <i>way</i> short of that.<br><br><br><br><i>you can also find my reviews at my blog</i><br>
  <a href="http://elfswood.blogspot.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img alt="elfswood" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380435889i/880802.jpg" width="220 px" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="9844553949789557026" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1567270980" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1567270980?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781481426664" href="/book/show/20759393-poison-princess">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=what-the-hell-was-that">what-the-hell-was-that</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1567270980" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6636638443141010526"><br/>Unpopular opinion review time!<br/><br/>You know how it goes: you loved this book, I didn’t. I’m actually very much dismayed by that, because I stepped into this apocalyptic world with such an overall optimistic state of mind – hell, I expected my first book by Kresley Cole, a <i>New York Times</i> bestseller, to be a winner!<br/><br/>Oh boy. My state of mind shifted quickly enough and darkened considerably. <br/><br/>Basically, I didn’t like anything about this book. It’s a huge “It’s not you; it’s me’’ case, so huge that I would </span>
  <span id="freeText6636638443141010526" style="display:none"><br />Unpopular opinion review time!<br /><br />You know how it goes: you loved this book, I didn’t. I’m actually very much dismayed by that, because I stepped into this apocalyptic world with such an overall optimistic state of mind – hell, I expected my first book by Kresley Cole, a <i>New York Times</i> bestseller, to be a winner!<br /><br />Oh boy. My state of mind shifted quickly enough and darkened considerably. <br /><br />Basically, I didn’t like anything about this book. It’s a huge “It’s not you; it’s me’’ case, so huge that I would have blamed the book entirely if it wasn’t for the glowing ratings and reviews. I totally would have.<br /><br />Because this was awful for me. <br /><br />Evie is one of the most superficial, spoiled and completely annoying heroines I’ve had the misfortune to meet. And the love interest, Jackson is a despicable pervert and jackass! Every time he called Evie “bébé,’’ my soul died a little. <br /><br />I have nothing against the French word for baby, but when Jackson pronounces that word, it doesn’t come out as sexy and enticing. It physically hurts and I wished I could punch that word out of his vocabulary. And I’m taking Karate classes, so I’m pretty confident about my blows. Just saying.<br /><br />I also couldn’t believe how many clichés the author inserted. I mean <i>come on</i>, this was supposed to be a post-apocalyptic enticing story!<br /><br />Clichés: <br /><br />- the superpopularandprettygirl who think of school as her kingdom (<i>‘‘I waved at different folks again and again, much to the bowheads’ amusement. I was pretty much friends with everybody’’</i>)<br />- the jackass love interest who acts like a jerk around Evie but he’s so handsome, so handsome, so handsome, and no one can resist him. Also very troubled and broken.<br />- the love triangle<br />- parents dead (this seems to become so common in YA books that it’s just one more trope to me)<br />- the jackass bad-boy rescues the lost superpopularandprettygirl<br /><br />And so on and so forth and what have you.<br /><br />The idea of people incarnating figures from tarot cards to save the world also didn’t appeal to me. I found the overall plot weird. It tries too hard to become something exceptional, when it really just isn’t.<br /><br />Oh well, and I bought the whole series, silly me. Guess I’ll have to host a giveaway soon.<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/hitormissbooks" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/hitormissbooks/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> <br /></span>

<div id="review_295216181" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/295216181" />
    <a title="Donna {Book Passion For Life}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3024878-donna-book-passion-for-life"><img alt="Donna {Book Passion For Life}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563622982p2/3024878.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/295216181?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna {Book Passion For Life}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna {Book Passion For Life}" href="/user/show/3024878-donna-book-passion-for-life">Donna {Book Passion For Life}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781442436657" href="/book/show/17164644-poison-princess">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024878-donna-book-passion-for-life?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024878-donna-book-passion-for-life?shelf=ya-dystopian-scifi-thriller">ya-dystopian-scifi-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer295216181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1392456002964346893"><b>“If you touch me like that again, Evangeline,” he began in a husky tone, dropping to his seat once more, “in the space of a heartbeat, I will have you off this bike and onto the closest horizontal surface. And I woan be picky, no.” </b><br/><br/>Oh for the love of all things holy, this book is amazing! This was my first book by author Kresley Cole and honestly she couldn't have done it any better. She had me compelled from the very first page with her amazing talent for storytelling and also for her intense a</span>
  <span id="freeText1392456002964346893" style="display:none"><b>“If you touch me like that again, Evangeline,” he began in a husky tone, dropping to his seat once more, “in the space of a heartbeat, I will have you off this bike and onto the closest horizontal surface. And I woan be picky, no.” </b><br /><br />Oh for the love of all things holy, this book is amazing! This was my first book by author Kresley Cole and honestly she couldn't have done it any better. She had me compelled from the very first page with her amazing talent for storytelling and also for her intense and incredible scenes. It's safe to say, <i>Poison Princess</i> is a gripping page turner! <br /><br />This story follows the life of teenager Evangeline 'Evie' Greene. She's a popular girl, with a loving boyfriend and awesome friends, but even though her life appears to be normal, it's anything but. Evie experiences hallucinations but mostly they are disturbing and horrifying. Not only that but Evie also gets visions of people that she's never met and they come with warnings. But soon it's to late for Evie to figure these warnings out because her hometown - including the rest of the world has been hit by an apocalyptic event called 'The Flash' where most people are wiped out. <br /><br />Evie is among the survivors and soon enough she finds out that the one person she hates is alive - Jackson. Evie needs answers about her visions and decides she needs to travel to see her grandmother - who she thinks is still alive. Jackson agrees to protect Evie on her mission but as her visions get worse, she soon comes across other people who have been having the same call, and she realises she is not the only who is meant to play out their destiny. <br /><br />Let me tell you right now, this book is so unique! Twenty two teens who all have special powers based on their characteristics of their Tarot card, so they can play their part in an ancient prophesy between good vs evil. Come on, tell me how unique that is? Honestly, I've not read anything like this book before and I'm still in awe with how brilliant it really is. <br /><br />Evie is a strong protagonist - one I instantly loved. She has the weight of the world on her shoulders and still she tries to remain upbeat, happy and generally tries to stay sane. Even after the flash, she tries to remain the same even though as Jackson points out on a number of occasions, she can't hunt, start fires or protect herself - but you know there's something bubbling under the surface of Evie and it's just waiting to be unleashed. At time's my heart broke for her because whatever is happening to her, she has no control over and at time's it's very scary. I'm glad she had a person like Jackson to lean on because without him, I think she would have struggled. <br /><br />Now Jackson, oh gosh, he's a complete bayou boy through and through and with him being Cajun French he has one hell of a sexy accent. However, he can be so harsh and mean sometimes and yes, he does do stupid things but really, you can over look everything because he's a total sweetheart at heart. It was pretty clear from the start that he was attracted to Evie - despite how he acts and even in the end, he'll always go to her. Their relationship is pretty intense, I was just waiting for something to happen. <br /><br />Then, that ending comes in and no sooner than you started....it's all finished...I could have cried. If this book wasn't unputdownable to start with, wait until you get to the last few chapters because it's even worse. I couldn't stop reading until I knew the outcome and my god, I was not expecting what I got. It was absolutely breath-taking and heart-breaking all at the same time. I'm left with so many questions because of that ending - it really was a killer, and I'm dying for more of this wonderful story. <br /><br />Overall, Kresley Cole has leaped into the YA market by a storm and it's left me wanting more of her work. I urge you guys to go buy this book because it's not one you want to miss out on. A must read of 2012! <br /><br /><b>A big thank you to Simon &amp; Schuster UK for giving me the opportunity to review this book.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="1392456002964346893" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText11761437448240569166" style="display:none"><b>Spoilers</b><br /><br />I couldn't be bothered writing a review, so you'll have to make do with this nonsensical rubbish:<br /><br /><b>Evie</b>: Woe is me. <div id="review_370288456" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/370288456" />
    <a title="Katie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1343589-katie"><img alt="Katie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486578421p2/1343589.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/370288456?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie" href="/user/show/1343589-katie">Katie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer370288456" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10162439623383527281">This is a tough book to review because there is a lot to like here. The concept behind the book is great, and I loved watching the puzzle pieces unfold, guessing who was who, seeing their powers in action, taking note of the symbolism, etc. But there are definitely some big problems with the book, which make it hard for me to recommend it.<br/><br/>The first chapter is intriguing, but then we're subjected to many boring pages of life before the Flash. The apocalyptic event mentioned on the back of the boo</span>
  <span id="freeText10162439623383527281" style="display:none">This is a tough book to review because there is a lot to like here. The concept behind the book is great, and I loved watching the puzzle pieces unfold, guessing who was who, seeing their powers in action, taking note of the symbolism, etc. But there are definitely some big problems with the book, which make it hard for me to recommend it.<br /><br />The first chapter is intriguing, but then we're subjected to many boring pages of life before the Flash. The apocalyptic event mentioned on the back of the book and in the first chapter doesn't happen until page 105 or so (in the ARC). That's 100 pages of Evie going to school, arguing with Jackson, having visions, thinking she's crazy, etc. Basically, the book could have started on page 100, because we really didn't need all that backstory before getting to the exciting stuff.<br /><br />Once the event actually happens things really pick up and I couldn't put the book down. There's the usual surviving the apocalypse stuff, which is fun, but there's also a very unique element here, one that I'm a particular fan of. But since it isn't listed on the back cover I don't want to spoil it - which is ironic, since I would never have picked up this book if I hadn't known about this twist before-hand.<br /><br />Unfortunately, the book suffers from weak, or downright repulsive, characters. Evie is pretty bland and pathetic for most of the book, and I wish that she'd had some useful skill or something. But then again, I'd probably be a lot like her (terrified, useless) if the apocalypse happened, so I could still relate to her.<br /><br />But the worst character was the love interest Jackson. I'm not sure I have ever disliked a love interest in a book so much. He drinks whiskey constantly. He beats people to pulps with his fists. He's horrible to the autistic kid. And with Evie he acts like a horny stalker, treats her like a possession, verbally abuses her, and pressures her to have sex with him throughout the entire book.<br /><br />An actual quote from Jackson (ARC, page 241): "Hell, Evie, you're probably the last girl on earth for me. Would it KILL you to put out?" And trust me, this isn't the only quote like this. I could go on and on. I kept waiting for Jackson to redeem himself, but if anything he only gets worse.<br /><br />Is this the kind of guy we want teen girls to fall in love with? I was so happy that Evie didn't put up with his crap most of the time, but SO disappointed she fell in love with him anyway. I wanted to put the book down because I was so disgusted by him, but I was so intrigued by the premise I kept reading anyway. I'm still on the fence about reading the next books.<br /><br />In a time when Goodreads reviews are being called "bullying" I'm very hesitant to post this review at all. But I seriously hope Jackson is made less of an ass before the book actually comes out, because otherwise it was very enjoyable. The author is definitely talented and has a lot of great stuff in this book, but Jackson completely ruins it. I'd love to recommend the book to everyone, but right now I can't.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10162439623383527281" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6496081634095160006">I did not finish this book...there were several things towards the beginning of the story that just had me laughing, it was so ludicrous. For example, the Big Bad Cajun Motorcycle Gang (also known as the Sharks and the Jets...oh, wrong story). They speak in heavily-accented Cajun patois, they have bikes with stolen, mismatched parts! They wear motorcycle jackets, their hair falls in greasy locks over their eyes! They rumble up to their new school in a crowd of big, bad, wolfery and start chattin</span>
  <span id="freeText6496081634095160006" style="display:none">I did not finish this book...there were several things towards the beginning of the story that just had me laughing, it was so ludicrous. For example, the Big Bad Cajun Motorcycle Gang (also known as the Sharks and the Jets...oh, wrong story). They speak in heavily-accented Cajun patois, they have bikes with stolen, mismatched parts! They wear motorcycle jackets, their hair falls in greasy locks over their eyes! They rumble up to their new school in a crowd of big, bad, wolfery and start chatting up and soliciting all the pretty girls.<br /><br />Aside from the dirt-poor, uneducated, rude Cajun stereotyping and the clichéd bad boys, nevertheless, I could have tolerated the minor absurdity if there had been some promise to a compelling story, but no. I'm not going to waste my time.<br /><br />Here are a few quotes <i>very</i> early on in the story that made up my mind for me.<br /><br /><b>"Beside him was a couple on a bike—a kid in camo pants and a girl in a pleather miniskirt. The big boy helped her off the bike, easily swinging her up—</b><br /><b>'Wheh-hell,' Catherine said, 'good to know her panties are hot pink. Shocked she’s wearing them, actually. Classy with a capital K.'</b><br /><b>Mel nodded thoughtfully. 'I finally understand who buys vajazzling kits.'</b><br /><br />I foresee slut-shaming in the future. Not a fan.<br /><br /><b>"Then Weasel zeroed in on me with a smirk. 'Ain’t you dat jolie girl in dat Porsha?' His Cajun accent was as thick as any I’d ever heard. 'Turn around, you, and hike up dat dress, so I can tell for true.'"</b><br /><br />...really? REALLY?<br /><br /><b>"'You’re laughing at me?' He clenched those big, taped fists like he was just dying to hit something. Most likely my face.</b><br /><br /><b><i>'Tu p’tee pute,'</i> he sneered to my face. You little bitch."</b><br /><br />The above quotes came from the projected love interest. A violent, misogynistic asshole. No. No. I'm just not going to bother.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/271776433?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Letitia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Letitia" href="/user/show/4952315-letitia">Letitia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4952315-letitia?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4952315-letitia?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer271776433" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11799470629084533802">Rating: A+ ... Heat: Sweet<p>I was nervous and anxious and a tad apprehensive to read this book. Kresley Cole is one of my ABSOLUTE favorite authors. If she writes it, I will read it. As proven by the fact that the moment this was available to preorder – I did. And yet, as excessively excited as I was, I also worried. Needlessly, let me tell you. It rocked. It rolled. It annihilated my expectations. And reaffirmed exactly why Miz Cole is an auto-buy author for me.</p><p><em>Poison Princess</em> is not the same ol’</p></span>
  <span id="freeText11799470629084533802" style="display:none">Rating: A+ ... Heat: Sweet<p>I was nervous and anxious and a tad apprehensive to read this book. Kresley Cole is one of my ABSOLUTE favorite authors. If she writes it, I will read it. As proven by the fact that the moment this was available to preorder – I did. And yet, as excessively excited as I was, I also worried. Needlessly, let me tell you. It rocked. It rolled. It annihilated my expectations. And reaffirmed exactly why Miz Cole is an auto-buy author for me.</p><p><em>Poison Princess</em> is not the same ol’ YA schtick. There are no vampires, werewolves, or angels to be had. Not a one. Instead, the twenty two cards of the Major Arcana tarot deck come to life—the Empress, the Magician, Death, etc., each of which possess unique powers and abilities—in a post-apocalyptic world. </p><p>Told both Before Flash and After Flash, there are two distinct tones and settings. </p><p>Before Flash is a world that feels very ‘of the times,’  where the teens act like teens. They’re not idealized. Some of them cuss, or drink, or smoke—and (gasp!) some of them are even having sex. And, as our heroine—Evie Greene—is from a well-to-do family, they have expensive tastes. Flashy clothes, fast cars. Skies the limit. Which served as an extreme juxtaposition for the world After Flash. Putting the characters at a bigger disadvantage, giving them more things to overcome. </p><p>After Flash, when the world has been ravaged by what could be solar flares (or not…), when anyone unlucky enough to be outside was turned into ash (or worse…), life is no longer easy and is filled with myriad <em>hard</em> limits. Limited food. Limited survivors. Limited women. Militias form, cannibalism becomes a reality, and slavers begin stealing people. It’s a very gritty and murky life for a teenager to be faced with.</p><p>And, oh my goodness, does Evie have a lot to overcome. She was, quite simply, a great heroine. She never truly frustrated me. She's not stupid, she's not weak. Thrust into tough situations time and again, she has to <em>learn</em> how to survive in a setting that comes with a steep learning curve. To say she struggles would be an understatement. But, c'mon. She's sixteen. She went from pampered rich girl to scavenger and survivor. She's going to make mistakes. She's not automatically going to be a she-woman survivalist who can skin animals with her teeth and kill people without a second thought. It felt real, and it felt right. She’s human, she’s resourceful—she isn’t infallible. </p><p>Then there is Jackson Deveaux (aka the Cajun I am now ragin' for). He’s used to fighting and constantly having to protect himself from danger. He’s a survivor. Rough around the edges and more than a little bit crass, he can come across mean at times. But his meanness comes from a hurt and damaged place deep inside. And, really, him and Evie spar verbally pretty equally. She delivers some barbs herself. The tension and animosity between them doesn’t rest solely on his shoulders. Besides, as a whole, I see him as simply trying to toughen her up. Give her a thicker skin. Actually give her a fighting chance in this new post-apocalyptic world. </p><p>Jack and Evie made my heart pang. The road they’re forced to walk down is <em>hard.</em> A constant battle. Life or death. It’s an extreme situation that brings out both the best and worst in them—as well as in the secondary characters. The cast of this book as a whole is fantastic. Guys and gals alike. Supernatural or simply human. The good and the evil. They’re all so vivid and unique and <em>interesting</em>. I’m invested in them and their journey and outcome 100%.</p><p>Which is probably why I stayed up till 3:30a to finish this. There was no good stopping point. No moment where things slowed down. I had to keep going, had to know what happened next. And the ending… it left me breathless. I was so keyed up and full of sympathy adrenaline that sleep evaded me for nearly an hour. Scenes from the book kept popping into my head.</p><p><em>Poison Princess</em> is full of myths and magic. Unrelenting action. Drama. Romance. It plays out in your head like a movie. Makes you invest. Care. It throws curves at you - some real humdingers – and keeps you guessing. Miz Cole has written such an energetic and dynamic story that both teens and adults will be captivated. It has, quite simply, ensnared my mind and my heart.</p><p>And the second book cannot come out soon enough! I want it. Bad. The wait, it’s going to be torture. I expect I’ll be rereading this one over and over, between releases, like I do Miz Cole’s other books.</p><p>
  <b>Favorite Quote: </b>
</p><blockquote> <p><i>I had to know what the look in his eyes promised.<br />He was staring at my lips, and before I could think better of it, I'd wetted them.<br />"That's it, bébé," he said in a coaxing rasp. "Ma bonne fille." My good girl.<br />He wrapped one of his arms behind my back, cupping my chin with his free hand.<br />"Evangeline, I'm goan to kiss you until your toes curl, until we're breathing for each other."<br />That was the promise...</i></p> </blockquote><br /><br /><b>
  <i> -- A <a href="http://romanticbookaffairs.blogspot.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Romantic Book Affairs</a> Review.<br /><br />Find us on <a href="https://twitter.com/rombookaffairs" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> and <a href="http://facebook.com/rombookaffairs" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> too!</i>
</b><br /></span>

<div id="review_288263988" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/288263988" />
    <a title="shady boots" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4972138-shady-boots"><img alt="shady boots" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592459241p2/4972138.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/288263988?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="shady boots" class="user" itemprop="url" name="shady boots" href="/user/show/4972138-shady-boots">shady boots</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=meh-it-was-okay">meh-it-was-okay</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=dont-understand-why-its-hyped">dont-understand-why-its-hyped</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=hot-mess">hot-mess</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer288263988" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13377251908693646624"><b>Edit (04/01/2018): Commentary from Present Day Me</b><br/><br/>So I've been revisiting some of my old reviews, thinking I might do some commentary for them in like, a self-reflection kinda way or just for a good laugh, and... wow this one is pretty cringey. It'd be wrong of me to adjust it I guess since this was just proof of what I was like as a teenager I suppose, so I'm gonna leave it untouched. <br/><br/>However, I do vividly remember this book and how awful and disgusting the hero was in it. It's kind of interesti</span>
  <span id="freeText13377251908693646624" style="display:none"><b>Edit (04/01/2018): Commentary from Present Day Me</b><br><br>So I've been revisiting some of my old reviews, thinking I might do some commentary for them in like, a self-reflection kinda way or just for a good laugh, and... wow this one is pretty cringey. It'd be wrong of me to adjust it I guess since this was just proof of what I was like as a teenager I suppose, so I'm gonna leave it untouched. <br><br>However, I do vividly remember this book and how awful and disgusting the hero was in it. It's kind of interesting to see how many people defended his actions in the comments. Says a lot about our culture at the time glorifying all these horrible men. I wonder if we're still like that today? Hopefully we've changed.<br><br><br><b>My old review (12/31/2012)</b><br><br>Actual rating is <b>2.5</b> stars. Or 2.75, not sure. Just lower than 3.<br><br>For the first time ever, I might just <i>only</i> be talking about the love interest in this review. Because I have so much to say about him. Well, maybe I'll talk about him 98% of the time or so, but believe you me, I will rip this guy apart and say everything that's on my mind about him, so prepare yourselves.<br><br>So, Jackson Deveaux. Ladies and gentleman, the unthinkable has happened. I've finally found a guy who is far far worse than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12578077.Obsidian__Lux___1_" title="Obsidian (Lux, #1) by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">Obsidian</a>'s Daemon Black. I had thought no one would ever take away his title has the most horrible YA love interest of all time, but apparently I was wrong.<br><br>I'll just give you a list of what this guy is:<br><br>- Arrogant<br>- Selfish<br>- Abusive<br>- Violent<br>- Perverted<br>- Rude<br>- A bully<br>- Has no regards for the main character's feelings<br>- Will sleep with any living thing that has a vagina<br>- Controlling<br>- Has anger issues<br><br>Any positive traits? Well... he's protective? More like possessive, really. Add <i>that</i> to the list, too. The author was smart, though. She added his Cajun accent and uses specific words when he's sweet-talking Evie. Like, "Let me take care of you, <i>bébé</i>." The author <i>knew</i> that girls love guys with accents. So I'm guessing that's why most of these girls are swooning for him.<br><br>This guy is a horrible human being. From the first half of the book, that was very clear, yet I didn't mind because I thought the main character dealt with him well. Not as well as I wish, but she was aware that he was nothing but a perverted bully, regardless of how hot he was.<br><br>But then by the second half, my god, this guy became even more disgusting. He constantly wants to get into Evie's pants, and he even <i>admits</i> it! Evie asked him if all he wanted was to get in her pants, and <i>he said yes</i>. In one scene he was about to do so but Evie refused, and I'd like to give you a direct quote he said from that scene, verbatim.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Hell, Evie, you're probably the last girl on earth for me. Would it kill you to put out?"</i>
</blockquote><br><br>And I'd like to show you what he said a few minutes after this scene, where they meet Selena, the "Other Girl" character.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Jackson turned to me with a devilish smile. In French, he said, "All of a sudden, Evie, you're not the last girl on earth for me."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Guess what happened that same night? He had sex with her. And he called Evie a "miserable tease". And near the end, after they got into <i>another</i> big fight, guess what Evie catches him doing afterwards. Making out with Selena.<br><br>I think Jackson Deveaux is a horrible, disgusting human being (and I've NEVER used the word 'disgusting' to describe a love interest before, but I think it suits him perfectly), and it boggles my mind that the author expects girls to actually swoon for him. I mean, WHAT THE FUCK? Even <i>Daemon</i> wasn't this bad. At least he cared about Katy's feelings. Jackson, however, doesn't give a shit about Evie's. Even when she's crying because of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[her mother dying <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> he's <i>yelling</i> at her. <br><br>All through this book, I was begging, BEGGING for a love triangle, and I got it, but it was for Jackson, and it wasn't even a love triangle. More like a sex triangle. Because that's all he's after, is sex! He freely admitted it! -_- What in the world was the author thinking, creating such a disgusting love interest?! And he's the main love interest, too. He's definitely costed this book a lot of stars in the rating, and I'm not sure I even want to continue this series because of him.<br><br>Okay, I think I got that off my chest. Ugh, I would suggest you all avoid this book simply because of him, because really, he's the worst.<br><br>Some quick thoughts on other things of the book, I liked the paranormal aspect, and how it was mixed with post-apocalyptic. Evie wasn't that bad of a heroine either, though she's way too soft and dependent. She's the popular cheerleader type, sure, but I would've liked if she had a sarcastic &amp; badass personality, like for example Alona from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7008041.The_Ghost_and_the_Goth__The_Ghost_and_the_Goth___1_" title="The Ghost and the Goth (The Ghost and the Goth, #1) by Stacey Kade" rel="nofollow noopener">The Ghost and the Goth</a>. If that were the case, then her and Jackson could have nice witty banter. But most of the time they just argue and yell at each other.<br><br>I also liked the ending. Initially I liked this book, but Jackson really really turned me off. I guess I'd give the sequel a try. *sigh* I just desperately hope there's a new love interest, because Jackson doesn't deserve to be one. He's a scumbag and a perv, and whoever <i>likes</i> him needs mental help. Like, go to the Dr. Phil show or something, seriously. Or better yet get your brain checked. I'd be genuinely concerned about your mental health.<br><br>I think I've said all I wanted to say. I'm going to finish off this review with some GIF messages for the lovely Mr. Jackson Deveaux.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380371444ra/724502.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380371444ra/724503.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380371444ra/724504.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/643914.gif" height="190" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That's all. c: Thank you.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_2342406656" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk"><img alt="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597641717p2/66224803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2342406656?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk">Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2342406656" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2604081354223032872"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1522581839ra/25305785.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i> "Come touch...but you'll pay a price. </i><br/><br/>Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br/>When my wonderful friend <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/65577580-marysscript' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mary</a> told me about a series that includes Tarot cards my interest was caught instantly. <br/>Tarot cards always had something mystic and mysterious about them that I loved. <br/>I started this book with high anticipation, lots of expectations and a really good mood. <br/>And first the book was awesome. It was a funny, entertaining book and Evie was an interesting character. But then the Flash happened and Evie became this whiny mess.</span>
  <span id="freeText2604081354223032872" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1522581839ra/25305785.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i> "Come touch...but you'll pay a price. </i><br><br>Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>When my wonderful friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/65577580-marysscript" rel="nofollow noopener">Mary</a> told me about a series that includes Tarot cards my interest was caught instantly. <br>Tarot cards always had something mystic and mysterious about them that I loved. <br>I started this book with high anticipation, lots of expectations and a really good mood. <br>And first the book was awesome. It was a funny, entertaining book and Evie was an interesting character. But then the Flash happened and Evie became this whiny mess. <br>And then a lot of things happened and she met a lot of people and with every page near the end it got more interesting.<br>Don’t get me wrong, I never really had a clue what’s going on or what would happen, but the love story and Evie as the main character made it “okay”. <br>But it was still so good that I continued and even finished it (that’s probably a wonder). <br>So... I’ll continue, I’m sure of it. First of all because Mary loved it and second because I can’t wait to see Evie becoming a super badass with her powers! <br>You go girl! <br><br>Characters ⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>I started this book with great characters, a sassy best friend and a love interest that caught my interest. <br>But reading the book I was annoyed with Evie and her whiny I-can’t-take-care-of-myself-attitude and Jackson’s cocky selfloving and sexist personality. <br>The only thing that got me going was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/65577580-marysscript" rel="nofollow noopener">Mary</a> telling me there will be awesome characters, and real cool side characters appearing in the story. <br>There are badass women, dangerous boys and cute boyish future looking boys. <br>All in all I wasn’t really satisfied with the main characters, but the side characters made the story better. <br><br>World ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1522582098ra/25305810.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Throughout my life I watched and read a lot of magical fantasy series. There were vampires, werewolves and witches. <br>But you know what never appears a lot in this series? Tarot cards. <br>And that’s the main thing happening in this book. Reincarnated tarot cards with magical powers that fight each other after the world ended in a flash. <br>Before the flash Evie had nightmares, delusions and hallucinations about people she never met that had magical powers and looked like tarot cards she saw at her grandmothers place. She saw plants growing near her and visions about a evil red witch. <br><br>Relationships ⭐️⭐️<br>No, no, no, just no. <br>Jackson - aka the main love interest - is probably the most annoying sexist asshole I have ever read of. He is protective, mean and super discouraging. There’s only a few moments where I slightly liked him. Only. A. Few. <br>So, I’m pretty disappointed about this part. <br>But, I mean, Jack could be sweet if he wanted to... <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i> "Evie, if you ever get taken from me again, you better know that I'll be coming for you."<br>He cupped my face with a bloodstained hand. <br>"So you stay the hell alive! You don't do like Clotile, you doan take that way out. <br>You and me can get through anything, just give me a chance."<br>--his voice broke lower <br>"just give me a chance to get to you." <br>He buried his face in my hair, inhaling deeply. <br>"There is nothing that can happen to you that we can't get past." </i>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Writing style ⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>The writing was really entertaining, but sadly it hasn't many quotable phrases. <br>Still it had a good pacing with a lot of action, magic and love.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="2604081354223032872" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1819074877" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12598786533918877186"><i> Buddy read with the wonderful, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5743835-brittany' rel='nofollow noopener'>Brittany</a> </i><br/><br/><b> <i> DNF @ 30% </i> </b><br/><br/>Looking at other people’s reviews has me very concerned . . . are we reading the same book or ???<br/><br/><i> Poison Princess </i> is about sixteen year old Evie Greene and her abilities in a post-apocalyptic world? I dunno, The plot is kinda hazy in my head. Instead, I was more focused on the characters and their douchebag qualities. <br/><br/>Allow me to elaborate. <br/><br/><i> Note: Evie is recounting her story to a literal psychopath –she doesn’t know –so she’s telling about </i></span>
  <span id="freeText12598786533918877186" style="display:none"><i> Buddy read with the wonderful, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5743835-brittany" rel="nofollow noopener">Brittany</a> </i><br /><br /><b> <i> DNF @ 30% </i> </b><br /><br />Looking at other people’s reviews has me very concerned . . . are we reading the same book or ???<br /><br /><i> Poison Princess </i> is about sixteen year old Evie Greene and her abilities in a post-apocalyptic world? I dunno, The plot is kinda hazy in my head. Instead, I was more focused on the characters and their douchebag qualities. <br /><br />Allow me to elaborate. <br /><br /><i> Note: Evie is recounting her story to a literal psychopath –she doesn’t know –so she’s telling about her life before the Flash </i><br /><br /><b> <i> Jackson McDouchebag Daniels: </i> </b><br />-	Calls her a b*tch to her face<br />-	Tries to kiss her (at her birthday party) when her boyfriend is a few feet away<br />-	Says crap like, “Maybe I came back to claim my taste of you.”<br />-	“You doan even know me, and you’re angling for another . . . podna?” (That’s a quote – yes it’s an accent – <i> sooooooo </i> hot, right?)<br />-	But we’ll forgive him cause:<br />-	“sunlight beamed through the window, striking his handsome face, highlighting his gray eyes and chiseled features.”<br />-	“With those cheekbones, squared jaw, and raven-black hair”<br /><br />:) I think you understand my problem with Mr. Insufferable.<br /><br /><b> <i> Mellissa Bestie Warren </i> </b><br />-	“Mel was over at my house, prepping me for date night because she felt the need to sluttify my outfit so I could stand a chance against Clotile’s “free-balling lady lumps.”<br />-	Yep, that’s a quote<br />-	“Eves, on the scale from wholesome to whoresome, you’re practically Amish.”<br />-	 “So what are you going to do about Brandon’s hymen safari?”<br />-	Nice to have a best friend that supports you in your choices, huh? :)<br /><br />And we’re not going to even go into the self-pitying, self-absorbed weakling that is the main character. Bye, Felicia. <br /><br />I’m sorry, but I did not find any redeeming qualities about the book, nor could I stand to read any more of this. <br /><br /><s> 0 stars (is that a thing? It should be) fine, fine, </s><br /><br />1 star!!</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3345867491" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer7257299128756381784"><a href='https://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/><b>DNF @ 49% </b><br/><br/><br/><br/>I actually felt kind of sorry for this book. It came out when everyone was starting to get sick of TWILIGHT and its ilk, so people really weren't feeling all that kindly towards paranormal romances with insipid heroines and emotionally controlling heroes. Maybe if it had come out today, when dystopians and paranormals are starting to have a resurgence, people would be kinder. But hey, sometimes you draw the short straw in publi</span>
  <span id="freeText7257299128756381784" style="display:none"><a href="https://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br><b>DNF @ 49% </b><br><br><br><br>I actually felt kind of sorry for this book. It came out when everyone was starting to get sick of TWILIGHT and its ilk, so people really weren't feeling all that kindly towards paranormal romances with insipid heroines and emotionally controlling heroes. Maybe if it had come out today, when dystopians and paranormals are starting to have a resurgence, people would be kinder. But hey, sometimes you draw the short straw in publishing trends and someone always has to be the last one.<br><br><b> </b><br><br>Set in Louisiana, POISON PRINCESS is the story of Evie, an ordinary high school student who's well-liked and part of the pretty set. Their lives are disrupted when a group of Cajun students join the school, poor and declasse, but undeniably attractive, and portrayed with every stereotype in the book. Their ringleader is a guy named Jackson who talks like a dirty 40-year-old man in a bar trapped in the ripped body of an 18-year-old.<br><br><br><br>But Evie has a secret. She sees visions-- dark, terrifying visions that she draws on her sketchbook. Visions of the end of the world. And then one day, it all comes to fruition and suddenly there's plagues, zombies, and worse, and all of the plants in the world just die. Except that Evie can grow them with her blood and maybe has a couple other superpowers up her sleeve, including the power to smell like a flower even when she's not wearing perfume! WOW!!!! Step aside, Superman.<br><br><br><br>I could probably make it through the whole book if I wanted to. I don't, because it isn't wowing me and I don't really feel invested enough to make myself continue. I personally didn't think it was as bad as some of my friends did, and found myself feeling more bemused than angry with the book. Jackson is a skeeve, yes, which is maybe why the author felt the need to include an incel serial killer who keeps girls locked up in his basement for experimentation and sex... you know, for contrast.<br><br><br><br>POISON PRINCESS is dark and while that can be a good thing in YA, I'm not really sure the author fully knew what she wanted from this world she created and it shows in the writing.<br><br><br><br>1.5 to 2 stars</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dana Kenedy (Dana and the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dana Kenedy (Dana and the Books)" href="/user/show/372001-dana-kenedy-dana-and-the-books">Dana Kenedy (Dana and the Books)</a>
